      1 # AgentBook — MVP Implementation Plan for A3P
      2 
      3 ## Overview
      4 
      5 AgentBook is an agent-based accounting system implemented as a se
        t of A3P plugins. Rather than a single monolithic plugin, the MVP
         is decomposed into **four cooperating plugins** that map to the 
        core accounting domains. Each plugin registers its own tools, con
        straints, and routes while sharing a common data layer through th
        e A3P plugin framework.
      6 
      7 This approach lets each domain evolve independently, enables gran
        ular permissions, and follows the A3P plugin-per-domain architect
        ure principle.
      8

⏺ Write(agentbook/agentbook.md)
  ⎿  Added 440 lines, removed 94 lines
       1  # AgentBook — MVP Implementation Plan for A3P
       2  
       3 +> **Governing documents:** This plan MUST be implemented in com
         +pliance with:                                                  
       4 +> - `architecture.md` — Component design, quality system, data 
         +architecture                                                   
       5 +> - `SKILL.md` — Code patterns, constraints, testing standards,
         + LLM prompt standards                                          
       6 +> - `requirements-v2.md` — Feature requirements, competitive po
         +sitioning, acceptance criteria                                 
       7 +> - `phased-plan.md` — Phase sequencing, exit criteria, risk re
         +gister                                                         
       8 +                                                               
       9 +---                                                            
      10 +                                                               
      11  ## Overview
      12  
       5 -AgentBook is an agent-based accounting system implemented as a 
         -set of A3P plugins. Rather than a single monolithic plugin, the
         - MVP is decomposed into **four cooperating plugins** that map t
         -o the core accounting domains. Each plugin registers its own to
         -ols, constraints, and routes while sharing a common data layer 
         -through the A3P plugin framework.                              
      13 +AgentBook is an agent-based accounting system implemented as a 
         +set of A3P plugins. Rather than a single monolithic plugin, the
         + MVP is decomposed into **four cooperating plugins** that map t
         +o the core accounting domains, plus an **agent framework** with
         + a decoupled **skill system** that allows the agent to be upgra
         +ded by improving skills without changing the framework.        
      14  
      15  This approach lets each domain evolve independently, enables gr
          anular permissions, and follows the A3P plugin-per-domain archi
          tecture principle.
      16  
      17  ---
      18  
      19 +## Agent Architecture: Framework + Skills (Decoupled)          
      20 +                                                               
      21 +### Design Principle                                           
      22 +The agent framework is a **generic orchestration engine**. All 
         +domain knowledge lives in **loadable, updatable skills**. The s
         +ystem can be iterated/upgraded by improving agent skills withou
         +t changing the agent framework.                                
      23 +                                                               
      24 +### Agent Framework (stable, rarely changes)                   
      25 +```                                                            
      26 +AgentFramework/                                                
      27 +  ├── orchestrator.ts        # Intent routing, DAG planning, ex
         +ecution loop                                                   
      28 +  ├── constraint-engine.ts   # Hard gates, escalation gates, so
         +ft checks                                                      
      29 +  ├── verifier.ts            # Independent verification pass   
      30 +  ├── context-assembler.ts   # Typed context loading per intent
      31 +  ├── escalation-router.ts   # Human-in-the-loop routing       
      32 +  ├── skill-registry.ts      # Discovers, loads, validates, hot
         +-reloads skills                                                
      33 +  └── event-emitter.ts       # Kafka event emission            
      34 +```                                                            
      35 +                                                               
      36 +### Skill System (evolves independently)                       
      37 +```                                                            
      38 +skills/                                                        
      39 +  ├── skill-manifest.json    # Declares: name, version, tools, 
         +constraints, prompts                                           
      40 +  ├── expense-recording/                                       
      41 +  │   ├── skill.json         # Tool definitions, input/output s
         +chemas, constraints                                            
      42 +  │   ├── prompts/           # Versioned prompt templates (inte
         +nt parsing, categorization)                                    
      43 +  │   ├── handlers/          # Tool execution logic            
      44 +  │   └── tests/             # Skill-specific test suite       
      45 +  ├── invoice-creation/                                        
      46 +  ├── tax-estimation/                                          
      47 +  ├── report-generation/                                       
      48 +  ├── bank-reconciliation/                                     
      49 +  └── ...                                                      
      50 +```                                                            
      51 +                                                               
      52 +### Skill Manifest Schema                                      
      53 +```json                                                        
      54 +{                                                              
      55 +  "name": "expense-recording",                                 
      56 +  "version": "1.2.0",                                          
      57 +  "description": "Record, categorize, and manage expenses",    
      58 +  "intents": ["record_expense", "categorize_expense", "edit_exp
         +ense"],                                                        
      59 +  "tools": [                                                   
      60 +    {                                                          
      61 +      "name": "record_expense",                                
      62 +      "inputSchema": { ... },                                  
      63 +      "outputSchema": { ... },                                 
      64 +      "constraints": ["balance_invariant", "amount_threshold"],
      65 +      "compensation": "void_expense",                          
      66 +      "modelTier": "haiku"                                     
      67 +    }                                                          
      68 +  ],                                                           
      69 +  "prompts": {                                                 
      70 +    "intent_parse": { "version": "1.3", "file": "prompts/intent
         +-parse.md" },                                                  
      71 +    "categorize": { "version": "2.1", "file": "prompts/categori
         +ze.md" }                                                       
      72 +  },                                                           
      73 +  "dependencies": ["agentbook-core"]                           
      74 +}                                                              
      75 +```                                                            
      76 +                                                               
      77 +### Skill Lifecycle                                            
      78 +- **Discovery:** Framework scans `skills/` directory on startup
      79 +- **Validation:** Each skill manifest is validated against the 
         +skill schema                                                   
      80 +- **Registration:** Tools, constraints, and prompts registered 
         +in the skill registry                                          
      81 +- **Hot-reload:** Skills can be updated at runtime without rest
         +arting the framework                                           
      82 +- **Versioning:** Multiple skill versions can coexist; A/B test
         +ing supported                                                  
      83 +- **Specialization:** New accounting specializations (e.g., Can
         +adian tax, EU VAT, crypto) are added as new skills, not framewo
         +rk changes                                                     
      84 +                                                               
      85 +---

          - that period

      504  ## Technical Decisions
      505  
      506  ### All amounts stored as integer cents
      193 -No floating-point in the financial path. `$45.99` → `4599`. Ro
          -unding applied only at display.                               
      507 +No floating-point in the financial path. `$45.99` -> `4599`. R
          +ounding applied only at display. Per SKILL.md: "all financial 
          +calculations use Decimal (not float), rounded to 2 decimal pla
          +ces."                                                         
      508  
      509  ### Constraint engine is code, not prompts
      196 -The LLM proposes; the constraint engine validates. Balance che
          -cks, period gates, and amount thresholds are deterministic cod
          -e that cannot be bypassed.                                    
      510 +The LLM proposes; the constraint engine validates. Per SKILL.m
          +d: "Never put accounting constraints inside LLM prompts as ins
          +tructions. Constraints are code, not text."                   
      511  
      512  ### Verification is a separate pass
      199 -After execution, a separate LLM call with an adversarial promp
          -t ("find errors in this entry") validates the result before co
          -mmit.                                                         
      513 +Per architecture.md: "The executor and the verifier are separa
          +te reasoning passes with separate prompts." The verifier's pro
          +mpt is adversarial: "Your job is to find errors."             
      514  
      515  ### Plugin-specific Prisma schemas
      202 -Each plugin owns its own PostgreSQL schema (`plugin_agentbook_
          -core`, `plugin_agentbook_expense`, etc.) for clean isolation w
          -hile sharing the same database.                               
      516 +Each plugin owns its own PostgreSQL schema for clean isolation
          + while sharing the same database.                             
      517  
      518 +### Agent framework / skill decoupling                        
      519 +The agent framework is generic orchestration. All domain knowl
          +edge lives in skills. Skills are versioned, hot-reloadable, an
          +d independently testable. IRS rate changes = skill update, not
          + framework change.                                            
      520 +                                                              
      521  ### LLM cost budget
      205 -- Intent parsing + categorization: Haiku tier (~$0.002/call)  
      206 -- Planning + verification: Sonnet tier (~$0.01/call)          
      207 -- Target: < $5/month per active tenant at 100 transactions/mon
          -th                                                            
      522 +Per architecture.md AD-6: Haiku tier for parsing/categorizatio
          +n, Sonnet tier for planning/verification. Target: < $5/month p
          +er active tenant at 100 transactions/month.

⏺ Update(agentbook/agentbook.md)
  ⎿  Added 2 lines
      12  
      13  AgentBook is an agent-based accounting system implemented as a 
          set of A3P plugins. Rather than a single monolithic plugin, the
           MVP is decomposed into **four cooperating plugins** that map t
          o the core accounting domains, plus an **agent framework** with
           a decoupled **skill system** that allows the agent to be upgra
          ded by improving skills without changing the framework.
      14  
      15 +**The MVP ships with full support for the United States and Can
         +ada.** The architecture is jurisdiction-aware from day one so t
         +hat adding new countries (UK, EU, Australia, etc.) requires onl
         +y a new **jurisdiction pack** — a bundle of tax rules, chart-of
         +-accounts templates, form generators, and locale config — with 
         +zero changes to the core framework, plugins, or database schema
         +.                                                              
      16 +                                                               
      17  This approach lets each domain evolve independently, enables gr
          anular permissions, and follows the A3P plugin-per-domain archi
          tecture principle.
      18  
      19  ---

⏺ Update(agentbook/agentbook.md)
  ⎿  Added 150 lines
       86  
       87  ---
       88  
       89 +## Multi-Jurisdiction Architecture (US + Canada, extensible)  
       90 +                                                              
       91 +### Design Principle                                          
       92 +Every component that touches tax rules, form generation, chart
          +-of-accounts defaults, sales tax, fiscal year conventions, or 
          +locale formatting is **parameterized by jurisdiction**. The co
          +re framework and plugins never contain hardcoded US or Canadia
          +n logic — they delegate to a **jurisdiction pack** loaded at t
          +enant configuration time.                                     
       93 +                                                              
       94 +### What varies by jurisdiction                               
       95 +                                                              
       96 +| Concern | US | Canada | Abstraction |                       
       97 +|---------|-----|--------|-------------|                      
       98 +| Income tax form | Schedule C (1040) | T2125 (T1) | `TaxFormG
          +enerator` interface |                                         
       99 +| Self-employment tax | SE tax (15.3%) | CPP/EI self-employed 
          +contributions | `SelfEmploymentTaxCalculator` interface |     
      100 +| Tax brackets | Federal + state progressive | Federal + provi
          +ncial progressive | `TaxBracketProvider` with year-versioned r
          +ates |                                                        
      101 +| Quarterly installments | Estimated tax (Apr/Jun/Sep/Jan) | Q
          +uarterly installments (Mar/Jun/Sep/Dec) | `InstallmentSchedule
          +` interface |                                                 
      102 +| Sales tax | State/county/city sales tax | GST (5%) + HST or 
          +PST by province | `SalesTaxEngine` interface |                
      103 +| Contractor reporting | 1099-NEC ($600 threshold) | T4A ($500
          + threshold) | `ContractorReportGenerator` interface |         
      104 +| Chart of accounts defaults | Schedule C line-aligned | T2125
          + category-aligned | `ChartOfAccountsTemplate` per jurisdiction
          + |                                                            
      105 +| Currency | USD | CAD | `tenant_config.currency` + multi-curr
          +ency amounts |                                                
      106 +| Fiscal year | Calendar year (most sole props) | Calendar yea
          +r (most sole props) | `tenant_config.fiscal_year_start` |     
      107 +| Mileage rate | IRS standard ($0.70/mile 2025) | CRA rate ($0
          +.72/km first 5000, $0.66 after) | `MileageRateProvider` with y
          +ear-versioned rates |                                         
      108 +| Receipt language | English | English + French | `locale` on 
          +tenant config |                                               
      109 +| Deduction categories | Home office (simplified/regular), Sec
          +tion 179 | Business-use-of-home, CCA classes | `DeductionRuleS
          +et` per jurisdiction |                                        
      110 +                                                              
      111 +### Jurisdiction Pack Structure                               
      112 +                                                              
      113 +A jurisdiction pack is a **skill bundle** that plugs into the 
          +agent's skill registry. Adding a new country = adding a new pa
          +ck. No framework or plugin changes required.                  
      114 +                                                              
      115 +```                                                           
      116 +jurisdiction-packs/                                           
      117 +  ├── us/                                                     
      118 +  │   ├── pack.json              # Declares: jurisdiction_id, 
          +supported_regions, tax_year                                   
      119 +  │   ├── tax-brackets/          # Federal + 50 state bracket 
          +tables (JSON, year-versioned)                                 
      120 +  │   ├── sales-tax/             # State/county rate tables   
      121 +  │   ├── forms/                                              
      122 +  │   │   ├── schedule-c.ts      # Implements TaxFormGenerator
      123 +  │   │   ├── schedule-se.ts     # Implements SelfEmploymentTa
          +xCalculator                                                   
      124 +  │   │   ├── form-1099-nec.ts   # Implements ContractorReport
          +Generator                                                     
      125 +  │   │   └── quarterly-estimates.ts  # Implements Installment
          +Schedule                                                      
      126 +  │   ├── chart-of-accounts.json # Default CoA template (Sched
          +ule C aligned)                                                
      127 +  │   ├── deductions.json        # Deduction rules (home offic
          +e, Section 179, etc.)                                         
      128 +  │   ├── mileage-rates.json     # IRS rates by year          
      129 +  │   └── prompts/               # US-specific prompt overlays
          + for categorization                                           
      130 +  │                                                           
      131 +  ├── ca/                                                     
      132 +  │   ├── pack.json                                           
      133 +  │   ├── tax-brackets/          # Federal + 13 province/terri
          +tory bracket tables                                           
      134 +  │   ├── sales-tax/             # GST/HST/PST rates by provin
          +ce                                                            
      135 +  │   ├── forms/                                              
      136 +  │   │   ├── t2125.ts           # Implements TaxFormGenerator
      137 +  │   │   ├── cpp-ei.ts          # Implements SelfEmploymentTa
          +xCalculator                                                   
      138 +  │   │   ├── t4a.ts             # Implements ContractorReport
          +Generator                                                     
      139 +  │   │   └── quarterly-installments.ts  # Implements Installm
          +entSchedule                                                   
      140 +  │   ├── chart-of-accounts.json # Default CoA template (T2125
          + aligned)                                                     
      141 +  │   ├── deductions.json        # CRA deduction rules (busine
          +ss-use-of-home, CCA)                                          
      142 +  │   ├── mileage-rates.json     # CRA rates by year          
      143 +  │   └── prompts/               # Canadian-specific prompt ov
          +erlays                                                        
      144 +  │                                                           
      145 +  └── _template/                 # Copy this to add a new coun
          +try                                                           
      146 +      ├── pack.json                                           
      147 +      └── README.md              # Instructions for implementi
          +ng each interface                                             
      148 +```                                                           
      149 +                                                              
      150 +### Jurisdiction Interfaces (implemented by each pack)        
      151 +                                                              
      152 +```typescript                                                 
      153 +// Every interface is parameterized by tax_year for annual rat
          +e updates                                                     
      154 +                                                              
      155 +interface TaxBracketProvider {                                
      156 +  jurisdiction: string;              // "us" | "ca" | "uk" | .
          +..                                                            
      157 +  region?: string;                   // state/province/nil    
      158 +  getTaxBrackets(taxYear: number): TaxBracket[];              
      159 +  calculateTax(taxableIncome: number, taxYear: number): TaxCal
          +culation;                                                     
      160 +}                                                             
      161 +                                                              
      162 +interface SelfEmploymentTaxCalculator {                       
      163 +  calculate(netSelfEmploymentIncome: number, taxYear: number):
          + {                                                            
      164 +    amount: number;                                           
      165 +    deductiblePortion: number;      // US: half of SE tax; CA:
          + enhanced CPP                                                 
      166 +    breakdown: Record<string, number>;                        
      167 +  };                                                          
      168 +}                                                             
      169 +                                                              
      170 +interface SalesTaxEngine {                                    
      171 +  getRates(region: string): SalesTaxRate[];                   
      172 +  calculateTax(amount: number, region: string): SalesTaxResult
          +;                                                             
      173 +  getFilingDeadlines(region: string, taxYear: number): Date[];
      174 +}                                                             
      175 +                                                              
      176 +interface TaxFormGenerator {                                  
      177 +  formId: string;                    // "schedule-c" | "t2125"
          + | ...                                                        
      178 +  generate(ledgerData: LedgerSummary, taxYear: number): TaxFor
          +mData;                                                        
      179 +  exportPDF(formData: TaxFormData): Buffer;                   
      180 +  exportMachineReadable(formData: TaxFormData): string; // TXF
          +, EFILE, etc.                                                 
      181 +}                                                             
      182 +                                                              
      183 +interface InstallmentSchedule {                               
      184 +  getDeadlines(taxYear: number): InstallmentDeadline[];       
      185 +  calculateAmount(method: string, yearToDateIncome: number, pr
          +iorYearTax: number): number;                                  
      186 +}                                                             
      187 +                                                              
      188 +interface ContractorReportGenerator {                         
      189 +  threshold: number;                 // US: 600, CA: 500      
      190 +  formId: string;                    // "1099-nec" | "t4a"    
      191 +  generate(contractorPayments: ContractorPayment[], taxYear: n
          +umber): ContractorReport[];                                   
      192 +}                                                             
      193 +                                                              
      194 +interface ChartOfAccountsTemplate {                           
      195 +  getDefaultAccounts(businessType: string): Account[];        
      196 +  getTaxCategoryMapping(): Record<string, string>; // account 
          +-> tax form line                                              
      197 +}                                                             
      198 +                                                              
      199 +interface MileageRateProvider {                               
      200 +  getRate(taxYear: number, totalKmOrMiles: number): { rate: nu
          +mber; unit: 'mile' | 'km' };                                  
      201 +}                                                             
      202 +                                                              
      203 +interface DeductionRuleSet {                                  
      204 +  getAvailableDeductions(businessType: string): DeductionRule[
          +];                                                            
      205 +  calculateDeduction(rule: string, inputs: Record<string, numb
          +er>): number;                                                 
      206 +}                                                             
      207 +```                                                           
      208 +                                                              
      209 +### How it works at runtime                                   
      210 +                                                              
      211 +1. **Tenant onboarding:** User selects country + region (state
          +/province). Stored in `ab_tenant_config.jurisdiction` and `ab_
          +tenant_config.region`.                                        
      212 +2. **Pack loading:** The skill registry loads the jurisdiction
          + pack matching the tenant's config. All tax/form/sales-tax int
          +erfaces resolve to the pack's implementations.                
      213 +3. **Core plugins are jurisdiction-agnostic:** `agentbook-core
          +` stores journal entries, chart of accounts, and amounts in ce
          +nts. It never references Schedule C, T2125, GST, or any jurisd
          +iction-specific concept.                                      
      214 +4. **Tax plugin delegates:** `agentbook-tax` calls `TaxBracket
          +Provider.calculateTax()`, `SelfEmploymentTaxCalculator.calcula
          +te()`, etc. It doesn't know whether it's computing IRS or CRA 
          +taxes.                                                        
      215 +5. **Adding a new country:** Implement the interfaces in a new
          + pack directory. Register it. Done. Zero changes to framework,
          + plugins, or schema.                                          
      216 +                                                              
      217 +### Multi-currency support                                    
      218 +                                                              
      219 +- All amounts stored as integer cents in the **tenant's base c
          +urrency** (USD or CAD for MVP).                               
      220 +- Foreign currency transactions store both `amount_cents` (bas
          +e) and `original_amount_cents` + `original_currency` + `exchan
          +ge_rate`.                                                     
      221 +- Exchange rates fetched at transaction date from a rate provi
          +der.                                                          
      222 +- Reports always display in tenant base currency; drill-down s
          +hows original currency.                                       
      223 +- Adding a new base currency = adding a currency config, not a
          + schema change.                                               
      224 +                                                              
      225 +### What is NOT jurisdiction-specific (shared across all count
          +ries)                                                         
      226 +                                                              
      227 +- Double-entry ledger mechanics (debits = credits is universal
          +)                                                             
      228 +- Receipt OCR and expense categorization (LLM-based, locale-aw
          +are prompts)                                                  
      229 +- Invoice creation and PDF generation (template uses tenant lo
          +cale/currency)                                                
      230 +- Bank connection via Plaid (supports US + Canada natively)   
      231 +- Stripe payment processing (supports both countries)         
      232 +- Pattern memory and learning                                 
      233 +- Agent framework, skill registry, constraint engine, verifica
          +tion pass                                                     
      234 +- Audit trail and event sourcing                              
      235 +- Dashboard UI (renders jurisdiction-specific data via the pac
          +k)                                                            
      236 +                                                              
      237 +---                                                           
      238 +

⏺ Done. Here's what was added:

  Multi-Jurisdiction Architecture (US + Canada, extensible to any country):

  1. Jurisdiction Pack system — each country is a self-contained pack
  implementing 9 interfaces:
    - TaxBracketProvider (federal + state/province progressive brackets)
    - SelfEmploymentTaxCalculator (US: SE tax 15.3%; CA: CPP/EI)
    - SalesTaxEngine (US: state/county; CA: GST/HST/PST per province)
    - TaxFormGenerator (US: Schedule C/SE; CA: T2125)
    - InstallmentSchedule (US: Apr/Jun/Sep/Jan; CA: Mar/Jun/Sep/Dec)
    - ContractorReportGenerator (US: 1099-NEC $600; CA: T4A $500)
    - ChartOfAccountsTemplate, MileageRateProvider, DeductionRuleSet
  2. Adding a new country = zero framework changes. Copy _template/, implement
  the interfaces, register. Done.
  3. What's shared (not duplicated per country): double-entry ledger, OCR,
  pattern memory, bank connection (Plaid supports US+CA), Stripe, dashboard,
  agent framework, skill registry.
  4. All phase tasks, tests, and assessments updated to verify both US and CA
  paths.

          +]

      432 +Agent: ✅ Recorded. Journal entry posted.                     
      433 +```

      439 +       $67.50 — The Keg Steakhouse                            
      440 +       📅 Mar 22, 2026                                        
      441 +       Subtotal: $58.26 | Tax: $7.57 | Tip: $1.67             
      442 +       Category: Meals & Entertainment                        
      443 +       [✅ Correct] [📁 Change category] [✏️ Edit] [🏠 Personal
          +]                                                             
      444 +User: [taps ✅ Correct]                                       
      445 +Agent: ✅ Recorded. Receipt saved. Journal entry posted.      
      446 +```                                                           
      447 +                                                              
      448 +**Flow 3: Low confidence**                                    
      449 +```

      452 +       $347.00 — AMZN MKTP

      454 +       • Software & Subscriptions (25%)                       
      455 +       • Personal (13%)

          +r manually]                                                   
      457 +```                                                           
      458 +

      460 +```

      463 +       $89.50 — Amazon.com                                    
      464 +       Order #123-456-789

⏺ Pushed. Here's the key change:

  Phase 0 now ships the "wow" UX from day one:

  - Telegram bot fully operational with Grammy (webhook mode)
  - Receipt photo capture — send a photo in Telegram, get structured expense in
  < 10 seconds
  - OCR skill using Claude vision / Google Vision API — extracts amount, vendor,
   date, line items, tax/tip
  - 4 Telegram UX flows documented: text expense, receipt photo (hero flow),
  low-confidence confirmation, forwarded email receipt
  - Inline keyboard confirmations — [Correct] [Change category] [Edit]
  [Personal]
  - Confidence gating — blurry receipts trigger "are you sure?" instead of
  auto-recording wrong data
  - Receipt storage — S3 with tenant-isolated paths, linked to expense, viewable
   in web dashboard
  - Web drag-and-drop — same OCR pipeline accessible from dashboard
  - PDF/email receipts — forward an Amazon confirmation to the bot, it parses
  automatically

  Phase 1 is now refocused on refinement (92%+ OCR accuracy, batch processing,
  handwritten receipts) rather than building the foundation.

⏺ Now I have the full picture. The fundamental gap: the plan is reactive — agent
   waits for user to send receipts, ask questions, request reports. A real
  accounting firm doesn't wait. It reaches out with insights, warnings,
  reminders, and actions. This proactive behavior needs to be a core
  architectural component, not a Phase 3 afterthought.

  Let me add a Proactive Engagement Engine to the architecture and weave it into
   every phase.

⏺ Update(agentbook/agentbook.md)
  ⎿  Added 75 lines, removed 2 lines
      18  
      19  ---
      20  
      21 +## Core Design Philosophy: Your 24/7 Accounting Firm           
      22 +                                                               
      23 +> **AgentBook is not a tool you use. It is a professional that 
         +works for you.**                                               
      24 +>                                                              
      25 +> A great accounting firm doesn't wait for you to call. It moni
         +tors your bank activity, flags unusual charges, reminds you abo
         +ut upcoming deadlines, hunts for tax savings, follows up on ove
         +rdue invoices, and surfaces insights you didn't know to ask for
         +. AgentBook does the same — proactively, around the clock, via 
         +Telegram messages that feel like a thoughtful partner checking 
         +in.                                                            
      26 +>                                                              
      27 +> **The architecture has two equal halves:**                   
      28 +> 1. **Reactive path** — user sends a receipt, asks a question,
         + requests a report. Agent responds.                            
      29 +> 2. **Proactive path** — agent monitors data, detects opportun
         +ities/risks, initiates contact. User responds (or ignores).    
      30 +>                                                              
      31 +> Both paths use the same skill system, constraint engine, and 
         +verification pipeline. The proactive path is not a bolt-on — it
         + is a **first-class architectural component** built from Phase 
         +0.                                                             
      32 +                                                               
      33 +---                                                            
      34 +                                                               
      35  ## Agent Architecture: Framework + Skills (Decoupled)
      36  
      37  ### Design Principle
      24 -The agent framework is a **generic orchestration engine**. All 
         -domain knowledge lives in **loadable, updatable skills**. The s
         -ystem can be iterated/upgraded by improving agent skills withou
         -t changing the agent framework.                                
      38 +The agent framework is a **generic orchestration engine** with 
         +two execution modes: **reactive** (responding to user messages)
         + and **proactive** (self-initiated based on schedules, events, 
         +and data analysis). All domain knowledge lives in **loadable, u
         +pdatable skills**. The system can be iterated/upgraded by impro
         +ving agent skills without changing the agent framework.

     ...

       53 +### Proactive Engagement Engine (the differentiator)          
       54 +                                                              
       55 +This is the component that makes AgentBook feel like a profess
          +ional firm, not a passive app. It runs continuously alongside 
          +the reactive path.                                            
       56 +                                                              
       57 +**Architecture:**                                             
       58 +```                                                           
       59 +ProactiveEngine/                                              
       60 +  ├── scheduler.ts           # Cron-based triggers (daily dige
          +st, weekly review, deadline reminders)

          +changes in real-time                                          
       62 +  ├── insight-generator.ts   # LLM-powered analysis: detects o
          +pportunities, risks, anomalies

          + to avoid notification fatigue                                
       64 +  ├── delivery-manager.ts    # Routes notifications: Telegram,
          + web dashboard, email digest                                  
       65 +  └── engagement-tracker.ts  # Tracks which notifications user

       69 +

          +ed, invoice overdue | Kafka consumer on `agentbooks.execution_

          +ty, spending anomaly | Periodic LLM analysis of tenant ledger

       93 +**Anti-annoyance design:**

          +alerts 3x, reduce frequency

      914  ### Agent framework / skill decoupling
      915  The agent framework is generic orchestration. All domain knowl
           edge lives in skills. Skills are versioned, hot-reloadable, an
           d independently testable. IRS rate changes = skill update, not
            framework change.
      916  
      917 -### LLM cost budget                                           
      918 -Per architecture.md AD-6: Haiku tier for parsing/categorizatio
          -n, Sonnet tier for planning/verification. Target: < $5/month p
          -er active tenant at 100 transactions/month.                   
      917 +### LLM via Service Gateway (configurable, not hardcoded)     
      918 +AgentBook does NOT directly call LLM provider APIs. All LLM ca
          +lls route through the A3P **service-gateway** plugin, which pr
          +ovides:                                                       
      919 +- **Configurable LLM backend:** tenant or platform admin can s
          +witch between Claude, GPT, open-source models, or self-hosted 
          +inference — without changing AgentBook code                   
      920 +- **Model tier routing:** skill manifests declare `modelTier: 
          +"haiku" | "sonnet" | "opus"`. The service gateway maps tiers t
          +o concrete models based on its connector configuration        
      921 +- **API key management:** LLM provider keys stored in service-
          +gateway's secret vault, never in AgentBook plugins            
      922 +- **Cost tracking:** service-gateway meters per-request token 
          +usage, enabling per-tenant cost budgets                       
      923 +- **Fallback chain:** if primary provider is down, gateway can
          + failover to secondary (e.g., Claude -> GPT -> local)         
      924 +- **Rate limiting:** gateway enforces per-tenant LLM call budg
          +ets to prevent runaway costs                                  
      925  
      926 +```typescript                                                 
      927 +// AgentBook skill calls LLM via service-gateway, never direct
          +ly                                                            
      928 +const response = await gateway.llm({                          
      929 +  tier: 'haiku',                    // mapped to concrete mode
          +l by gateway config                                           
      930 +  tenant_id: context.tenant_id,                               
      931 +  prompt: categorization_prompt,                              
      932 +  max_tokens: 200,                                            
      933 +});                                                           
      934 +```                                                           
      935 +                                                              
      936 +**LLM cost budget target:** < $5/month per active tenant at 10
          +0 transactions/month (Haiku for parsing/categorization, Sonnet
          + for planning/verification).                                  
      937 +

⏺ Pushed. Here's the summary of both changes:

  Proactive Engagement Engine (the core differentiator)

  The plan now has a "Your 24/7 Accounting Firm" design philosophy at its
  foundation. The agent has two equal execution modes:

  1. Reactive — user sends receipt, asks question. Agent responds.
  2. Proactive — agent monitors data, detects opportunities/risks, initiates
  contact. User responds with one tap.

  Architecture components: scheduler (cron per tenant, timezone-aware), event
  watcher (Kafka), insight generator (LLM analysis), priority ranker
  (anti-annoyance), engagement tracker (feedback loop).

  Proactive messages by phase:
  - Phase 0: Daily pulse ("$340 in, $127 out"), receipt reminders, expense
  follow-ups
  - Phase 1: Invoice chase ("Acme 7 days overdue, send reminder?"), recurring
  anomalies ("Figma $59.99 instead of $49.99"), weekly review, payment
  celebrations
  - Phase 2: Tax deadline reminders (7/3 days before), deduction hunting ("no
  home office logged, save $1,500"), bank anomaly alerts, reconciliation nudges
  - Phase 3: Cash flow warnings ("balance drops to $1,200 on April 3"), spending
   trends, client payment predictions, monthly health report
  - Phase 4: Year-end optimization ("4 actions save $2,840"), 1099/T4A threshold
   warnings

  Anti-annoyance design: quiet hours, priority ranking, engagement-driven
  frequency tuning, snooze/dismiss, consolidation into digests, one-tap action
  buttons on every message.

  LLM via Service Gateway

  All LLM calls route through the A3P service-gateway plugin — AgentBook never
  calls LLM providers directly. This gives:
  - Configurable backend (Claude/GPT/open-source/self-hosted) without code
  changes
  - Model tier routing (skill declares haiku/sonnet, gateway maps to concrete
  model)
  - API keys in gateway's secret vault
  - Per-tenant cost tracking and rate limiting
  - Fallback chain if primary provider is down

✻ Brewed for 13m 39s

ready, so it makes multi-lang support very easy

       77 +### Calendar & Deadline Engine (always on the clock)          
       78 +                                                              
       79 +The agent maintains a **living calendar** of every date that m
          +atters for each tenant's financial life. This is not a simple 
          +reminder system — it is a jurisdiction-aware, tenant-scoped ca
          +lendar that auto-populates from the jurisdiction pack and adap
          +ts as the tenant's data changes.                              
       80 +                                                              
       81 +**Calendar sources (auto-populated per jurisdiction pack):**  
       82 +                                                              
       83 +| Source | US Examples | CA Examples |                        
       84 +|--------|-----------|-------------|                          
       85 +| **Government tax deadlines** | Apr 15 (annual), Jun 15/Sep 1
          +5/Jan 15 (quarterly), Jan 31 (1099 filing) | Apr 30 (annual), 
          +Mar 15/Jun 15/Sep 15/Dec 15 (installments), Feb 28 (T4A filing
          +) |

          + state | GST/HST: quarterly or annual by province |           
       87 +| **Fiscal quarter closes** | Q1: Mar 31, Q2: Jun 30, Q3: Sep 
          +30, Q4: Dec 31 | Same (configurable fiscal year) |            
       88 +| **Year-end critical dates** | Nov 1 (start tax optimization)
          +, Dec 31 (expense acceleration cutoff), Jan 15 (Q4 estimated t
          +ax) | Same pattern, different deadlines |                     
       89 +| **Market/financial dates** | Bank holidays (Fed Reserve cale
          +ndar), Stripe payout schedule | Bank holidays (Bank of Canada 
          +calendar), Interac schedule |                                 
       90 +| **Seasonal patterns** | Tax season (Feb-Apr), back-to-school
          +, holiday spending | Same + RRSP deadline (Mar 1) |           
       91 +                                                              
       92 +**Tenant-specific dates (auto-discovered from data):**        
       93 +                                                              
       94 +| Source | Examples |                                         
       95 +|--------|---------|                                          
       96 +| **Invoice due dates** | Client payment terms -> upcoming due
          + dates |                                                      
       97 +| **Recurring expense dates** | Subscription renewal dates (au
          +to-detected from pattern) |                                   
       98 +| **Contractor payment thresholds** | "Alex hits $600/$500 thr
          +eshold on next payment" |                                     
       99 +| **Client payment patterns** | "Acme typically pays 18 days a
          +fter invoice" -> expected payment date |                      
      100 +| **Cash flow crunch dates** | Projected dates where balance d
          +rops below threshold |                                        
      101 +                                                              
      102 +**Deadline data model:**                                      
      103 +```                                                           
      104 +ab_calendar_events (                                          
      105 +  id, tenant_id, jurisdiction,                                
      106 +  event_type,                    -- tax_deadline | filing_dead
          +line | quarter_close | market_holiday | tenant_custom         
      107 +  title,                         -- "Q2 Estimated Tax Due" (i1
          +8n key)                                                       
      108 +  date, time,                                                 
      109 +  lead_time_days,                -- when to start alerting (7 
          +days before, 3 days before, day-of)                           
      110 +  urgency,                       -- critical | important | inf
          +ormational                                                    
      111 +  action_url,                    -- deep link: IRS Direct Pay 
          +URL, CRA My Account, etc.                                     
      112 +  action_label,                  -- "Pay Now" (i18n key)      
      113 +  recurrence,                    -- annual | quarterly | month
          +ly | once                                                     
      114 +  source,                        -- jurisdiction_pack | invoic
          +e | pattern | user_custom                                     
      115 +  status                         -- upcoming | alerted | acted
          +_on | missed | snoozed                                        
      116 +)                                                             
      117 +```                                                           
      118 +                                                              
      119 +**How it works:**                                             
      120 +1. On tenant onboarding, jurisdiction pack seeds all governmen
          +t/tax deadlines for the tax year                              
      121 +2. As invoices are created, their due dates auto-populate the 
          +calendar                                                      
      122 +3. As patterns are detected (recurring expenses), renewal date
          +s are projected                                               
      123 +4. As bank data flows in, cash flow crunch dates are calculate
          +d                                                             
      124 +5. The proactive engine checks the calendar every hour, fires 
          +alerts at configured lead times                               
      125 +6. New tax year -> jurisdiction pack auto-seeds next year's de
          +adlines

  ⎿  Added 110 lines
      159  ```
      160  The engine learns: "This tenant acts on invoice reminders with
           in 2 hours but ignores spending anomaly alerts. Increase invoi
           ce reminder priority, reduce anomaly alert frequency."
      161  
      162 +---                                                           
      163 +                                                              
      164 +## Internationalization (i18n) — Built Into the Core          
      165 +                                                              
      166 +### Design Principle                                          
      167 +Every string the user sees — Telegram messages, web dashboard 
          +labels, proactive alerts, PDF reports, error messages, inline 
          +keyboard buttons — goes through the i18n layer. **No hardcoded
          + English strings in business logic or UI components.** This is
          + enforced from Phase 0, not retrofitted later.                
      168 +                                                              
      169 +### Architecture                                              
      170 +```                                                           
      171 +i18n/                                                         
      172 +  ├── core.ts                  # i18n runtime: t() function, l
          +ocale resolution, pluralization                               
      173 +  ├── locales/                                                
      174 +  │   ├── en/                  # English (default)            
      175 +  │   │   ├── common.json      # Shared: buttons, labels, erro
          +rs, units                                                     
      176 +  │   │   ├── expense.json     # "Receipt saved", "Category: {
          +category}", etc.                                              
      177 +  │   │   ├── invoice.json     # "Invoice #{number} sent to {c
          +lient}"                                                       
      178 +  │   │   ├── tax.json         # "Quarterly tax due: {amount}"
          +, "Deduction found: {description}"                            
      179 +  │   │   ├── proactive.json   # "Daily pulse: {in} in, {out} 
          +out", "Acme is {days} days overdue"                           
      180 +  │   │   └── reports.json     # P&L headers, balance sheet la
          +bels, column names                                            
      181 +  │   ├── fr/                  # French (Canadian French for M
          +VP)                                                           
      182 +  │   │   ├── common.json                                     
      183 +  │   │   ├── expense.json                                    
      184 +  │   │   └── ...                                             
      185 +  │   └── _template/           # Copy to add a new language   
      186 +  │       └── README.md                                       
      187 +  ├── types.ts                 # TypeScript type-safe i18n key
          +s (compile-time checking)                                     
      188 +  └── middleware.ts             # Resolves locale from tenant 
          +config for every request                                      
      189 +```                                                           
      190 +                                                              
      191 +### How it works                                              
      192 +                                                              
      193 +**1. Every user-facing string uses a translation key:**       
      194 +```typescript                                                 
      195 +// WRONG — hardcoded string                                   
      196 +await telegram.send("Receipt saved. Journal entry posted.");  
      197 +                                                              
      198 +// CORRECT — i18n key with interpolation                      
      199 +await telegram.send(t('expense.receipt_saved', { amount: forma
          +tCurrency(4500, locale) }));                                  
      200 +// en: "Receipt saved. $45.00 recorded."                      
      201 +// fr: "Recu enregistre. 45,00 $ enregistre."                 
      202 +```                                                           
      203 +                                                              
      204 +**2. Currency, date, and number formatting is locale-aware:** 
      205 +```typescript                                                 
      206 +formatCurrency(4500, 'en-US')  // "$45.00"                    
      207 +formatCurrency(4500, 'en-CA')  // "$45.00"  (CAD symbol same, 
          +but context differs)                                          
      208 +formatCurrency(4500, 'fr-CA')  // "45,00 $"  (comma decimal, s
          +ymbol after)                                                  
      209 +                                                              
      210 +formatDate(date, 'en-US')      // "Mar 22, 2026"              
      211 +formatDate(date, 'fr-CA')      // "22 mars 2026"              
      212 +                                                              
      213 +formatNumber(1234.56, 'en')    // "1,234.56"                  
      214 +formatNumber(1234.56, 'fr')    // "1 234,56"                  
      215 +```                                                           
      216 +                                                              
      217 +**3. Telegram inline keyboard buttons are i18n'd:**           
      218 +```typescript                                                 
      219 +// Buttons use translation keys                               
      220 +const keyboard = [                                            
      221 +  [{ text: t('common.correct'), callback_data: 'confirm' }],  
      222 +  [{ text: t('expense.change_category'), callback_data: 'chang
          +e_cat' }],                                                    
      223 +  [{ text: t('expense.mark_personal'), callback_data: 'persona
          +l' }],                                                        
      224 +];                                                            
      225 +// en: [Correct] [Change category] [Mark personal]            
      226 +// fr: [Correct] [Changer la categorie] [Marquer personnel]   
      227 +```                                                           
      228 +                                                              
      229 +**4. PDF reports and tax forms use locale-aware templates:**  
      230 +- Invoice PDFs: locale determines date format, currency format
          +, column headers                                              
      231 +- P&L reports: account names from jurisdiction pack (already l
          +ocalized), column labels from i18n                            
      232 +- Tax forms: generated by jurisdiction pack which includes loc
          +ale-specific field labels                                     
      233 +                                                              
      234 +**5. Proactive messages are fully i18n'd:**                   
      235 +```json                                                       
      236 +// proactive.json (en)                                        
      237 +{                                                             
      238 +  "daily_pulse": "Today: {income} in, {expenses} out. Cash bal
          +ance: {balance}. {action_count} items need attention.",       
      239 +  "invoice_overdue": "{client} is {days} days overdue on {amou
          +nt}. Send a reminder?",                                       
      240 +  "tax_deadline": "Quarterly tax payment due in {days} days. I
          + calculated {amount} for {quarter}."                          
      241 +}                                                             
      242 +                                                              
      243 +// proactive.json (fr)                                        
      244 +{                                                             
      245 +  "daily_pulse": "Aujourd'hui : {income} entrant, {expenses} s
          +ortant. Solde : {balance}. {action_count} elements necessitent
          + votre attention.",                                           
      246 +  "invoice_overdue": "{client} a {days} jours de retard sur {a
          +mount}. Envoyer un rappel ?",                                 
      247 +  "tax_deadline": "Paiement d'impot trimestriel du dans {days}
          + jours. J'ai calcule {amount} pour {quarter}."                
      248 +}                                                             
      249 +```                                                           
      250 +                                                              
      251 +**6. Locale resolution chain:**                               
      252 +1. Tenant config `locale` field (e.g., `fr-CA`) — primary     
      253 +2. User browser `Accept-Language` header — fallback for web   
      254 +3. Telegram user `language_code` — fallback for Telegram      
      255 +4. Default: `en`                                              
      256 +                                                              
      257 +### MVP languages                                             
      258 +- **`en`** — English (US + CA, default)                       
      259 +- **`fr`** — French (Canadian French, for Quebec users)       
      260 +                                                              
      261 +### Adding a new language                                     
      262 +1. Copy `i18n/locales/_template/` to `i18n/locales/{lang}/`   
      263 +2. Translate all JSON files (can be LLM-assisted with human re
          +view)                                                         
      264 +3. Register in locale config                                  
      265 +4. No code changes — the i18n runtime discovers new locales au
          +tomatically                                                   
      266 +                                                              
      267 +### Compile-time safety                                       
      268 +TypeScript types are auto-generated from the `en` locale files
          +. If a translation key is missing in any locale, the build war
          +ns. If code references a non-existent key, it fails at compile
          + time.                                                        
      269 +                                                              
      270 +---                                                           
      271 +                                                              
      272  ### Skill System (evolves independently)
      273  ```
      274  skills/

 using tools, not fixed config like traditional tools

      117 +- A new jurisdiction pack automatically brings its deadlines —

          +ects the next date — the calendar self-maintains              
      120 +- When market holidays change, the market-calendar skill fetch
          +es updated data — no code deploys                             
      121 +- Custom user dates ("remind me to invoice Acme on the 1st of 
          +each month") are just another skill adding events

⏺ Pushed. Here's what was added:

  Calendar & Deadline Engine (skill-driven, not config)

  The key difference from traditional tools: deadlines are discovered by skills 
  via CalendarProvider tools, not stored in hardcoded config files. Each skill
  that knows about dates registers a tool the calendar engine queries. This
  means:

  - Jurisdiction pack adds a new tax deadline -> calendar auto-updates on next
  skill refresh
  - Invoice created -> invoice skill adds due date to calendar
  - Recurring pattern detected -> expense skill projects renewal date
  - Bank sync reveals cash crunch -> cash flow skill adds warning date
  - New country jurisdiction pack -> its tax deadlines appear automatically

  Sources: government tax deadlines, sales tax filing, fiscal quarters, market
  holidays (Fed Reserve / Bank of Canada), Stripe payout schedules, seasonal
  patterns (tax season, RRSP deadline), invoice due dates, subscription
  renewals, client payment predictions, cash flow crunch dates.

  i18n — No Hardcoded Strings From Day One

  - t() function with interpolation and pluralization on every user-facing
  string
  - Locale-aware formatters: formatCurrency(4500, 'fr-CA') = "45,00 $",
  formatDate(date, 'fr-CA') = "22 mars 2026"
  - MVP languages: English + Canadian French (Quebec)
  - Compile-time safety: TypeScript types auto-generated from en locale —
  missing key = build error
  - Adding a new language: Copy _template/, translate JSON files, done. Zero
  code changes.
  - Everything i18n'd: Telegram messages, inline keyboard buttons, proactive
  alerts, calendar event titles, PDF report headers, error messages

           +t.js API routes at `/api/v1/agentbook/*` |

           +ame — imported as library, runs in serverless function |

           +ependencies |

           +Bundled at build time, same skill manifests |                
      1210 +| **Database** | Docker PostgreSQL | Vercel Postgres (Neon) w
           +ith PgBouncer pooling |                                      
      1211 +| **Telegram bot** | Webhook via ngrok | Webhook API route: `
           +/api/v1/agentbook/telegram/webhook` |                        
      1212 +| **Proactive engine (scheduler)** | Local cron process | **V
           +ercel Cron Jobs** (vercel.json `crons` config) |             
      1213 +| **Proactive engine (events)** | Kafka consumer | **Database
           + polling** + Vercel cron (no Kafka on Vercel) |              
      1214 +| **Receipt storage** | Local S3/MinIO | Vercel Blob Storage 
           +(BLOB_READ_WRITE_TOKEN) |                                    
      1215 +| **Event bus** | Kafka | Database-backed event table (append

      1255 +Note: Vercel cron fires in UTC. The cron handler resolves per
           +-tenant timezone and delivers at the correct local time (e.g.
           +, daily pulse at 8am tenant TZ, not 8am UTC).                
      1256 +                                                             
      1257 +**Event bus on Vercel (no Kafka):**                          
      1258 +                                                             
      1259 +Kafka is not available in Vercel serverless. The event bus ha
           +s a **dual-mode implementation:**                            
      1260 +- **Local dev:** Kafka producer/consumer (full event streamin
           +g)                                                           
      1261 +- **Vercel:** Database-backed append-only event table + polli
           +ng                                                           
      1262 +  - Events written to `ab_events` table (same Neon DB, `plugi
           +n_agentbook_core` schema)                                    
      1263 +  - Cron jobs poll for unprocessed events and trigger consume
           +rs                                                           
      1264 +  - Pattern memory, audit log, and analytics read from the ev
           +ent table                                                    
      1265 +  - The interface is identical — skills emit events the same 
           +way regardless of backend                                    
      1266 +                                                             
      1267 +```typescript                                                
      1268 +// Event emission — same interface, different backend        
      1269 +import { emitEvent } from '@agentbook/event-bus';            
      1270 +                                                             
      1271 +await emitEvent({                                            
      1272 +  type: 'expense.recorded',                                  
      1273 +  tenant_id: context.tenant_id,                              
      1274 +  payload: { expense_id, amount_cents, category_id },        
      1275 +});                                                          
      1276 +// Local: produces to Kafka topic                            
      1277 +// Vercel: inserts into ab_events table                      
      1278 +```                                                          
      1279 +                                                             
      1280 +**Telegram bot on Vercel:**                                  
      1281 +                                                             
      1282 +The Telegram bot runs as a **webhook**, not polling. This is 
           +serverless-compatible:                                       
      1283 +1. Register webhook URL with Telegram: `https://app.example.c
           +om/api/v1/agentbook/telegram/webhook`                        
      1284 +2. Telegram sends POST to this URL on every message          
      1285 +3. The API route handler processes the message, calls the age
           +nt framework, responds                                       
      1286 +4. Proactive messages (daily pulse, reminders) are sent via T
           +elegram Bot API from cron handlers

      1363  ### Verification is a separate pass

      1366 +### Plugin-specific Prisma schemas (single DB, multi-schema, 
           +serverless-compatible)                                       
      1367 +Each plugin owns its own PostgreSQL schema (`plugin_agentbook
           +_core`, `plugin_agentbook_expense`, etc.) within the single A
           +3P database. Prisma `multiSchema` preview feature handles sch
           +ema routing. The same Prisma client works on local Docker Pos
           +tgreSQL and Vercel Postgres (Neon) with PgBouncer connection 
           +pooling. Cross-schema relations (e.g., expense -> `public.Use
           +r`) work natively since all schemas are in the same database.
      1368  
      1369  ### Agent framework / skill decoupling
      1370  The agent framework is generic orchestration. All domain know
            ledge lives in skills. Skills are versioned, hot-reloadable, 
            and independently testable. IRS rate changes = skill update, 
            not framework change.

⏺ Pushed. Here's the summary:

  Deployment Architecture

  The key design decision: AgentBook has no separate backend processes in
  production. Everything runs as Next.js API routes (serverless functions) on
  Vercel, using the same deployment model as the rest of A3P.

  Database: Prisma Multi-Schema, Single DB
  - 4 new schemas (plugin_agentbook_core, _expense, _invoice, _tax) added to the
   existing A3P Prisma schema
  - Same Neon PostgreSQL database, PgBouncer connection pooling
  - DATABASE_URL (pooled) for queries, DATABASE_URL_UNPOOLED for migrations
  - Cross-schema relations work natively (e.g., expense references public.User)

  Vercel adaptations for components that need persistent processes:

  ┌──────────────────┬───────────────┬─────────────────────────────────────┐
  │    Component     │    Problem    │              Solution               │
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────┤
  │                  │ Needs to      │ Webhook API route (serverless, not  │
  │ Telegram bot     │ receive       │ polling)                            │
  │                  │ messages      │                                     │
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Proactive engine │ Needs cron    │ Vercel Cron Jobs (4 cron routes in  │
  │  (scheduler)     │ triggers      │ vercel.json)                        │
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Event bus        │ No Kafka on   │ Dual-mode: Kafka (local) / DB table │
  │ (Kafka)          │ Vercel        │  + polling (Vercel), same           │
  │                  │               │ emitEvent() interface               │
  ├──────────────────┼───────────────┼─────────────────────────────────────┤
  │ Receipt storage  │ Needs blob    │ Vercel Blob (production) / local    │
  │                  │ storage       │ filesystem (dev)                    │
  └──────────────────┴───────────────┴─────────────────────────────────────┘

  Build pipeline: No new steps — AgentBook integrates into existing
  vercel-build.sh (plugin builds -> prisma db push -> Next.js build).

⏺ The ralph-loop plugin is installed but needs to be activated. Based on the
  available skills I can see, the correct skill names are:

  - ralph-loop:ralph-loop — Start a Ralph Loop in current session
  - ralph-loop:cancel-ralph — Cancel an active Ralph Loop
  - ralph-loop:help — Explain Ralph Loop and available commands

  To use it, try these slash commands:

  /ralph-loop:help          # See how it works
  /ralph-loop:ralph-loop    # Start a loop
  /ralph-loop:cancel-ralph  # Stop a running loop

  If those don't work, try running /reload-plugins first to activate the
  recently installed plugin, then try again.

⏺ Ralph Loop needs a task to work on. It runs a prompt in a loop until
  completion. Usage:

  /ralph-loop <your task description>

  Examples:
  /ralph-loop Build the agentbook-core plugin scaffold
  /ralph-loop Fix the auth bug --max-iterations 20
  /ralph-loop --completion-promise 'DONE' Implement expense recording skill

  Options:
  - --max-iterations N — limit how many times the loop runs
  - --completion-promise 'TEXT' — stop when this text appears in output

  What task would you like Ralph Loop to work on?

      396 +// === Dashboard Snapshot (for Telegram sharing) ===          
      397 +app.post('/api/v1/agentbook-core/snapshot', async (req, res) =
          +> {                                                           
      398 +  try {                                                       
      399 +    const tenantId = (req as any).tenantId;                   
      400 +    const { type, data } = req.body;                          
      401 +                                                              
      402 +    // Generate a text-based financial highlight summary      
      403 +    // In Phase 3+, this will render an actual image via Puppe
          +teer/Playwright                                               
      404 +    const highlight = {                                       
      405 +      type: type || 'dashboard_highlight',                    
      406 +      tenant_id: tenantId,                                    
      407 +      generated_at: new Date().toISOString(),                 
      408 +      summary: data,                                          
      409 +      // The proactive engine can pick this up and send to Tel
          +egram                                                         
      410 +      // as a formatted message or rendered image             
      411 +      telegram_message: formatSnapshotMessage(data),          
      412 +    };                                                        
      413 +                                                              
      414 +    // Emit event so proactive engine can deliver to Telegram 
      415 +    await db.abEvent.create({                                 
      416 +      data: {                                                 
      417 +        tenantId,                                             
      418 +        eventType: 'snapshot.requested',                      
      419 +        actor: 'human',                                       
      420 +        action: highlight,                                    
      421 +      },                                                      
      422 +    });                                                       
      423 +                                                              
      424 +    res.json({ success: true, data: highlight });             
      425 +  } catch (err) {                                             
      426 +    res.status(500).json({ success: false, error: String(err) 
          +});                                                           
      427 +  }                                                           
      428 +});                                                           
      429 +                                                              
      430 +function formatSnapshotMessage(data: any): string {           
      431 +  const fmt = (cents: number) => {                            
      432 +    const amount = Math.abs(cents || 0) / 100;                
      433 +    const sign = (cents || 0) < 0 ? '-' : '';                 
      434 +    return `${sign}$${amount.toLocaleString('en-US', { minimum
          +FractionDigits: 2 })}`;                                       
      435 +  };                                                          
      436 +                                                              
      437 +  return [                                                    
      438 +    `📊 <b>Financial Snapshot</b>`,                           
      439 +    ``,                                                       
      440 +    `🏦 Cash: <b>${fmt(data?.assets)}</b>`,                   
      441 +    `📈 Revenue: ${fmt(data?.revenue)}`,                      
      442 +    `📉 Expenses: ${fmt(data?.expenses)}`,                    
      443 +    `💰 Net Income: <b>${fmt(data?.netIncome)}</b>`,          
      444 +    ``,                                                       
      445 +    data?.balanced ? `✅ Books balanced` : `⚠️ Books out of bal
          +ance`,                                                        
      446 +    ``,                                                       
      447 +    `<i>Generated ${new Date().toLocaleString()}</i>`,        
      448 +  ].join('\n');                                               
      449 +}                                                             
      450 +
